<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">University of Minnesota</h1>			<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">

<p>The <b>University of Minnesota, Twin Cities</b> (often referred to as the <b>University of Minnesota</b>, <b>Minnesota</b>, <b>the U of M</b>, <b>UMN</b>, or simply <b>the U</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public research university</a> in <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis" title="Minneapolis">Minneapolis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Paul,_Minnesota" title="Saint Paul, Minnesota">Saint Paul, Minnesota</a>.  The Minneapolis and St. Paul campuses are approximately 3 miles (4.8&#160;km) apart, and the Saint Paul campus is actually in neighboring <a href="/wiki/Falcon_Heights,_Minnesota" title="Falcon Heights, Minnesota">Falcon Heights</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> It is the oldest and largest campus within the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_system" title="University of Minnesota system">University of Minnesota system</a> and has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_university_campuses_by_enrollment" title="List of United States university campuses by enrollment">sixth-largest</a> main campus student body in the United States, with 51,848 students in 2017–18. The university is the <a href="/wiki/Flagship_university" class="mw-redirect" title="Flagship university">flagship</a> institution of the University of Minnesota system, and is organized into 19 colleges and schools, with sister campuses in <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_Crookston" title="University of Minnesota Crookston">Crookston</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_Duluth" title="University of Minnesota Duluth">Duluth</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_Morris" title="University of Minnesota Morris">Morris</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_Rochester" title="University of Minnesota Rochester">Rochester</a>.
</p><p>The University of Minnesota is one of America's <a href="/wiki/Public_Ivy" title="Public Ivy">Public Ivy</a> universities, which refers to top public universities in the United States capable of providing a collegiate experience comparable with the <a href="/wiki/Ivy_League" title="Ivy League">Ivy League</a>. Founded in 1851, The University of Minnesota is categorized as a Doctoral University - Highest Research Activity (R1) in the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Classification_of_Institutions_of_Higher_Education" title="Carnegie Classification of Institutions of Higher Education">Carnegie Classification of Institutions of Higher Education</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Minnesota is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> and is ranked 14th in research activity with $881 million in research and development expenditures in the fiscal year ending June 30, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The University of Minnesota faculty, alumni, and researchers have won <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_by_university_affiliation" title="List of Nobel laureates by university affiliation">29 Nobel Prizes</a><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> and three <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prizes" class="mw-redirect" title="Pulitzer Prizes">Pulitzer Prizes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
Notable University of Minnesota alumni include two Vice Presidents of the United States, <a href="/wiki/Hubert_Humphrey" title="Hubert Humphrey">Hubert Humphrey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Walter_Mondale" title="Walter Mondale">Walter Mondale</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">Bob Dylan</a>, who received the 2016  Nobel Prize in Literature.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization_and_administration">Organization and administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Organization and administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The university organization structure consists of 19 colleges, schools, and other major academic units:<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul><li>Center for Allied Health Programs</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_College_of_Biological_Sciences" title="University of Minnesota College of Biological Sciences">College of Biological Sciences</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/College_of_Continuing_and_Professional_Studies" title="College of Continuing and Professional Studies">College of Continuing and Professional Studies</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_School_of_Dentistry" title="University of Minnesota School of Dentistry">School of Dentistry</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota-Twin_Cities_College_of_Design" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Minnesota-Twin Cities College of Design">College of Design</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_College_of_Education_and_Human_Development" title="University of Minnesota College of Education and Human Development">College of Education and Human Development</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota_Extension&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="University of Minnesota Extension (page does not exist)">Extension</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_College_of_Food,_Agricultural_and_Natural_Resource_Sciences" title="University of Minnesota College of Food, Agricultural and Natural Resource Sciences">College of Food, Agricultural and Natural Resource Sciences</a></li>
<li>Graduate School</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_Law_School" title="University of Minnesota Law School">Law School</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_College_of_Liberal_Arts" title="University of Minnesota College of Liberal Arts">College of Liberal Arts</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Carlson_School_of_Management" title="Carlson School of Management">Carlson School of Management</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_Medical_School" title="University of Minnesota Medical School">Medical School</a></li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Institutes_and_centers">Institutes and centers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Institutes and centers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The university has six university-wide interdisciplinary centers and institutes whose work crosses collegiate lines:<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Center for Cognitive Sciences</li>
<li>Consortium on Law and Values in Health, Environment, and the Life Sciences</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Advanced_Study_at_University_of_Minnesota" title="Institute for Advanced Study at University of Minnesota">Institute for Advanced Study at University of Minnesota</a></li>
<li>Institute for Translational Neuroscience</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Institute_on_the_Environment" title="Institute on the Environment">Institute on the Environment</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Population_Center" title="Minnesota Population Center">Minnesota Population Center</a></li></ul>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Global">Global</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Global">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 2016, Minnesota was ranked 33rd in the world by the <i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a> (ARWU)</i>. In its 2017 edition, <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> ranked Minnesota 38th in their "Best Global University Rankings".<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a></i> for 2015 ranks Minnesota 46th in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The Center for World University Rankings (CWUR) ranked the university 35th in the world and 25th in the United States based on quality of education, alumni employment, quality of faculty, publications, influence, citations, broad impact, and patents in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, the Nature Index ranked Minnesota 34th in the world based on research publication output in top tier academic journals in the life sciences, chemistry, earth and environmental sciences and physical sciences based on publication data from 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, <i>Academic Ranking of World Universities</i> ranked the university 11th in the world for mathematics.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="National">National</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: National">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The University of Minnesota is ranked 14 overall among the nation's top research universities by the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Measuring_University_Performance" title="Center for Measuring University Performance">Center for Measuring University Performance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The university's <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a> expenditures ranked 13th-15th among U.S. academic institutions in the 2010 through 2015 <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a> reports.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> 2016 rankings placed the undergraduate program of the university as the 69th-best National University in the United States. It also ranked the Chemical Engineering program third-best, the Doctor of Pharmacy (PharmD) program third best, the Economics PhD program tenth, Psychology eighth, Statistics sixteenth, Audiology ninth, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_Medical_School" title="University of Minnesota Medical School">University of Minnesota Medical School</a> 6th for primary care and 34th for research.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_Law_School" title="University of Minnesota Law School">Law School</a>, consistently recognized as a 'Top Law School' by <a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a>, is ranked 20th in the nation, and is a national leader in <a href="/wiki/Commercial_law" title="Commercial law">commercial law</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a>, and clinical education.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, nineteen of the university's graduate-school departments have been ranked in the nation's top-twenty by the U.S. <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Research_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="United States National Research Council">National Research Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> In 2008 and 2012 <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i> ranked the College of Pharmacy 2nd in the nation. 2016 U.S. News &amp; Report now rank the College of Pharmacy 2nd in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i> ranked the School of Public Health 8th in the nation,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> which is home to the 2nd ranked program for the Master of Healthcare Administration degree.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The University of Minnesota ranked 19th in NIH funding in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>   
Minnesota is listed as a "<a href="/wiki/Public_Ivy" title="Public Ivy">Public Ivy</a>" in 2001 Greenes' Guides <i>The Public Ivies: America's Flagship Public Universities</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Discoveries_and_innovation">Discoveries and innovation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Discoveries and innovation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The university is known for innovation in research. The inventions by students and faculty have ranged from food science to health technologies. Most of the public research funding in Minnesota is funneled to the University of Minnesota as a result of long standing advocacy by the university itself.
</p><p>The university developed <a href="/wiki/Gopher_(protocol)" title="Gopher (protocol)">Gopher</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> a precursor to the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">World Wide Web</a> which used <a href="/wiki/Hyperlinks" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyperlinks">hyperlinks</a> to connect documents across computers on the internet. However, the version produced by <a href="/wiki/CERN" title="CERN">CERN</a> was favored by the public since it was freely distributed and could more easily handle multimedia webpages.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The university also houses the <a href="/wiki/Charles_Babbage_Institute" title="Charles Babbage Institute">Charles Babbage Institute</a>, a research and archive center specializing in computer history. The department has strong roots in the early days of supercomputing with Seymour Cray of Cray supercomputers.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The university also became a member of the Laser Interferometer Gravitational-wave Observatory (LIGO) in 2007, and has led data analysis projects searching for gravitational waves – the existence of which were confirmed by scientists in February 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-timeshighereducation.com_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeshighereducation.com-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Puffed_rice" title="Puffed rice">Puffed rice</a> – <a href="/wiki/Alexander_P._Anderson" title="Alexander P. Anderson">Alexander P. Anderson</a> led to the discovery of "puffed rice", a starting point for a new breakfast cereal later advertised as "Food Shot From Guns".</li>
<li>Transistorized cardiac pacemaker – <a href="/wiki/Earl_Bakken" title="Earl Bakken">Earl Bakken</a> founded Medtronic, where he developed the first external, battery-operated, transistorized, wearable artificial pacemaker in 1957.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ATP_synthase" title="ATP synthase">ATP synthase</a> – <a href="/wiki/Paul_D._Boyer" title="Paul D. Boyer">Paul D. Boyer</a> elucidated the enzymatic mechanism for synthesis of adenosine triphosphate (ATP), leading to a Nobel Prize in 1997.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Point-contact_transistor" title="Point-contact transistor">Point-contact transistor</a> – <a href="/wiki/Walter_Houser_Brattain" title="Walter Houser Brattain">Walter Houser Brattain</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Bardeen" title="John Bardeen">John Bardeen</a>, later joined by William Shockley, invented the point-contact transistor in December 1947. For their invention the trio was awarded a <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">Nobel Prize in Physics</a> in 1956.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Infusion_pump" title="Infusion pump">Infusion pump</a> – <a href="/wiki/Henry_Buchwald" title="Henry Buchwald">Henry Buchwald</a> invented world's first infusion port, peritoneovenous shunts, and specialty vascular catheters. He also invented the first implantable infusion pump, a precursor to implantable infusion pumps in use throughout the world today.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Photosynthesis" title="Photosynthesis">Photosynthesis</a> – <a href="/wiki/Melvin_Calvin" title="Melvin Calvin">Melvin Calvin</a> discovered the Calvin cycle along with Andrew Benson and James Bassham, for which he was awarded the 1961 Nobel Prize in Chemistry.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Supercomputer" title="Supercomputer">Supercomputer</a> – <a href="/wiki/Seymour_Cray" title="Seymour Cray">Seymour Cray</a>  designed a series of computers that were the fastest in the world for decades, and founded Cray Research which built many of these machines.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Taconite" title="Taconite">Taconite</a> – <a href="/wiki/Edward_Wilson_Davis" title="Edward Wilson Davis">Edward Wilson Davis</a> developed an engineering process to economically extract iron ore from hard taconite rocks, making taconite valuable as iron ore for the iron and steel industries.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cosmic_ray" title="Cosmic ray">Cosmic ray</a> – <a href="/wiki/Phyllis_S._Freier" title="Phyllis S. Freier">Phyllis S. Freier</a> discovered the presence of heavy nuclei in cosmic rays, proving the similarity between our solar system and the rest of the galaxy.</li>
<li>U.S. aviation – <a href="/wiki/Robert_Rowe_Gilruth" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert Rowe Gilruth">Robert Rowe Gilruth</a> led the development of flying qualities for airplanes, the use of rockets to achieve data at supersonic speeds and the establishment of many of the nation's leading flight research and human space flight operations facilities.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bone_marrow_transplant" class="mw-redirect" title="Bone marrow transplant">Bone marrow transplant</a> – <a href="/wiki/Robert_A._Good" title="Robert A. Good">Robert A. Good</a> performed the first successful human bone marrow transplant between persons who were not identical twins and is regarded as a founder of modern immunology.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gore-Tex" title="Gore-Tex">Gore-Tex</a> – <a href="/wiki/Robert_W._Gore" title="Robert W. Gore">Robert Gore</a> invents Gore-Tex materials in 1969.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Disk_drive" class="mw-redirect" title="Disk drive">Disk drive</a> – <a href="/wiki/Reynold_B._Johnson" title="Reynold B. Johnson">Reynold B. Johnson</a> invents method and machinery to score tests electronically.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/K-rations" class="mw-redirect" title="K-rations">K-rations</a> – <a href="/wiki/Ancel_Keys" title="Ancel Keys">Ancel Keys</a> patented in 1978, has become a widely prescribed drug for preventing heart disease and life-threatening arrhythmias.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Synthetic_rubber" title="Synthetic rubber">Synthetic rubber</a> – <a href="/wiki/Izaak_Kolthoff" title="Izaak Kolthoff">Izaak Kolthoff</a> developed the "cold process" for producing synthetic rubber, which he undertook under the U.S. synthetic rubber program during World War II.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cyclotron" title="Cyclotron">Cyclotron</a> – <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Lawrence" title="Ernest Lawrence">Ernest Lawrence</a> won the Nobel Prize for Physics 1939 for inventing and developing the cyclotron.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Drosophila_melanogaster" title="Drosophila melanogaster">Drosophila melanogaster</a> – <a href="/wiki/Edward_B._Lewis" title="Edward B. Lewis">Edward Lewis</a> discovered the Drosophila Bithorax complex of homeotic genes.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cardiac_surgery" title="Cardiac surgery">Cardiac surgery</a> – <a href="/wiki/C._Walton_Lillehei" title="C. Walton Lillehei">C. Walton Lillehei</a> pioneered open-heart surgery, as well as numerous techniques, equipment and prostheses for cardiothoracic surgery.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/POPmail" title="POPmail">POPmail</a> – <a href="/wiki/Mark_P._McCahill" title="Mark P. McCahill">Mark P. McCahill</a> led the development of the Gopher protocol, the effective predecessor of the World Wide Web, was involved in creating and codifying the standard for Uniform Resource Locators (URLs) and led the development of POPmail, one of the first e-mail clients which had a foundational influence on later e-mail clients and the popularization of graphical user interfaces in Internet technologies more broadly.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Multiphasic_Personality_Inventory" title="Minnesota Multiphasic Personality Inventory">MMPI</a> – <a href="/wiki/Starke_R._Hathaway" title="Starke R. Hathaway">Starke R. Hathaway</a> and <a href="/wiki/J._C._McKinley" title="J. C. McKinley">J. C. McKinley</a> created the Minnesota Multiphasic Personality Inventory (MMPI), which was first published in 1943.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zatocoding" class="mw-redirect" title="Zatocoding">Zatocoding</a> – <a href="/wiki/Calvin_Mooers" title="Calvin Mooers">Calvin Mooers</a> developed a mechanical system using superimposed codes of descriptors for information retrieval called Zatocoding.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Atomic_bomb" class="mw-redirect" title="Atomic bomb">Atomic bomb</a> – <a href="/wiki/Edward_P._Ney" title="Edward P. Ney">Edward P. Ney</a> discovered cosmic ray heavy nuclei and solar proton events. After early work involving separating isotopes from uranium, he worked on the Manhattan Project which created the first atomic bomb.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Atomic_bomb" class="mw-redirect" title="Atomic bomb">Atomic bomb</a> – <a href="/wiki/Alfred_O._C._Nier" title="Alfred O. C. Nier">Alfred O. C. Nier</a> devised a method to isolate uranium isotope, a critical discovery in the atomic age. Nier worked with <a href="/wiki/Kellex_Corporation" title="Kellex Corporation">Kellex Corporation</a> in New York City on the design and development of efficient and effective mass spectrographs for use in the Manhattan Project to build the atomic bomb in World War II. During the war most of the spectrographs used for monitoring uranium separations were designed by Nier.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Atomic_bomb" class="mw-redirect" title="Atomic bomb">Atomic bomb</a> – <a href="/wiki/Frank_Oppenheimer" title="Frank Oppenheimer">Frank Oppenheimer</a> worked on uranium isotope separation in 1945 and joined the Manhattan Project.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">Biotechnology</a> – <a href="/wiki/Ronald_L._Phillips" title="Ronald L. Phillips">Ronald L. Phillips</a>  was the first to generate whole corn plants from cells grown in culture, which laid the foundation for, and sparked, a new industry, using cell-culture methods to genetically modify corn plants and other cereals. The corn cell line which is most widely used for genetic modification of corn has greatly accelerated the improvement of corn, as food, feed and fuel.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">Renewable energy</a> – <a href="/wiki/Lanny_D._Schmidt" title="Lanny D. Schmidt">Lanny D. Schmidt</a> discovered a reactor to extract hydrogen from ethanol, offering the first real hope hydrogen could be a source of inexpensive and renewable energy.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Biomimetics" title="Biomimetics">Biomimetics</a> – <a href="/wiki/Otto_Schmitt" title="Otto Schmitt">Otto Schmitt</a> invented the Schmitt trigger, the cathode follower, the differential amplifier, and the chopper-stabilized amplifier.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> – <a href="/wiki/Deke_Slayton" title="Deke Slayton">Deke Slayton</a> was one of the original NASA Mercury Seven astronauts, and became NASA's first chief of the Astronaut Office.  He served as NASA's director of flight crew operations, making him responsible for crew assignments at NASA from November 1963 until March 1972. At that time he was granted medical clearance to fly, and was assigned as the docking module pilot of the 1975 Apollo–Soyuz Test Project, at age 51 becoming the oldest person to fly in space at the time.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bathythermograph" title="Bathythermograph">Bathythermograph</a> – <a href="/wiki/Athelstan_Spilhaus" title="Athelstan Spilhaus">Athelstan Spilhaus</a> fully developed the bathythermograph (BT) in 1938, an instrument he perfected was of vital importance in World War II in the battle against the German U-boat. During the war, the BT became standard equipment on all U.S. Navy subs and vessels involved in antisubmarine warfare.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/CDC_6600" title="CDC 6600">CDC 6600</a> – <a href="/w/index.php?title=James_E._Thornton&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="James E. Thornton (page does not exist)">James Thornton</a> developed the CDC 6600, the world’s first supercomputer, designed with Seymour Cray.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ziagen" class="mw-redirect" title="Ziagen">Ziagen</a> – <a href="/wiki/Robert_Vince_(scientist)" title="Robert Vince (scientist)">Robert Vince</a> worked on antiviral drug candidates at the University of Minnesota, where he went on to develop carbocyclic nucleosides termed 'carbovirs'. This class of medicinal agents included the drug abacavir. Abacavir was commercialized by GlaxoSmithKline as Ziagen for the treatment of AIDS.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campuses">Campuses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Campuses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As the largest of five campuses across the University of Minnesota system, its more than 50,000 students make it the sixth largest campus student body in the US overall. It has more than 300 research, education, and outreach centers and institutes, on everything from the life sciences to public policy and technology.<sup id="cite_ref-timeshighereducation.com_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeshighereducation.com-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The university offers 143 undergraduate degree programs<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> and 200 graduate degree programs.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The university has all three branches of the <a href="/wiki/Reserve_Officer_Training_Corps" class="mw-redirect" title="Reserve Officer Training Corps">Reserve Officer Training Corps</a> (ROTC).<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The University of Minnesota Twin Cities as well as its sister campuses at <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_Crookston" title="University of Minnesota Crookston">Crookston</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_Duluth" title="University of Minnesota Duluth">Duluth</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_Morris" title="University of Minnesota Morris">Morris</a> are accredited by the <a href="/wiki/Higher_Learning_Commission" title="Higher Learning Commission">Higher Learning Commission</a> (HLC).<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The racial/ethnic breakdown of the student population is: 65.3% White, 12.7% International Students (that are undesignated race/ethnicity), 9.2% Asian, 4.3% Black, 3.1% Hispanic/Latino, 1.2% American/Native American Indian, and 4.2% Unknown.  63% of matriculants to the university are considered Minnesota residents, and 37% of matriculants are considered out-of-state residents.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> According to the University Office of Institutional Research, as of Fall 2015, there are 30,511 undergraduates at the University of Minnesota Twin Cities campus. Of that number, 5,771 are first-time degree seeking freshmen. There are 12,659 graduate students.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Minneapolis_campus">Minneapolis campus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Minneapolis campus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The original Minneapolis campus overlooked the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Anthony_Falls" title="Saint Anthony Falls">Saint Anthony Falls</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a>, but it was later moved about a mile (1.6&#160;km) downstream to its current location. The original site is now marked by a small park known as Chute Square at the intersection of University and Central Avenues. The school shut down following a financial crisis during the American Civil War, but reopened in 1867 with considerable financial help from <a href="/wiki/John_S._Pillsbury" title="John S. Pillsbury">John S. Pillsbury</a>. It was upgraded from a <a href="/wiki/University-preparatory_school" class="mw-redirect" title="University-preparatory school">preparatory school</a> to a college in 1869.  Today, the university's Minneapolis campus is divided by the Mississippi River into an East and West Bank.
</p><p>The campus now has buildings on both river banks. The "<i>East Bank</i>", the main portion of the campus, covers 307 acres (124&#160;ha). The West Bank is home to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_Law_School" title="University of Minnesota Law School">University of Minnesota Law School</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Humphrey_School_of_Public_Affairs" title="Humphrey School of Public Affairs">Humphrey School of Public Affairs</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Carlson_School_of_Management" title="Carlson School of Management">Carlson School of Management</a>, various social science buildings, and the performing arts center. The St. Paul campus is home to the College of Biological Sciences (CBS), the College of Design (CDes), the College of Food, Agriculture and Natural Resource Sciences (CFANS), and the veterinary program.
</p><p>The Minneapolis campus has several residence halls, 17th Avenue Hall, Centennial Hall, Frontier Hall, Territorial Hall, Pioneer Hall, Sanford Hall, Middlebrook hall, and Comstock Hall.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="East_Bank">East Bank</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: East Bank">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Northrop_Mall_2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Northrop_Mall_2.JPG/220px-Northrop_Mall_2.JPG" width="220" height="106" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Northrop_Mall_2.JPG/330px-Northrop_Mall_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Northrop_Mall_2.JPG/440px-Northrop_Mall_2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="6641" data-file-height="3190" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Northrop_Mall_2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Northrop Mall</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Northrop_Mall_Winter.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Northrop_Mall_Winter.png/220px-Northrop_Mall_Winter.png" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Northrop_Mall_Winter.png/330px-Northrop_Mall_Winter.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Northrop_Mall_Winter.png/440px-Northrop_Mall_Winter.png 2x" data-file-width="1334" data-file-height="750" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Northrop_Mall_Winter.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>University of Minnesota East Bank campus in the winter</div></div></div>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:502px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Northrop_Mall_panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Northrop_Mall_panorama.jpg/500px-Northrop_Mall_panorama.jpg" width="500" height="114" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Northrop_Mall_panorama.jpg/750px-Northrop_Mall_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Northrop_Mall_panorama.jpg/1000px-Northrop_Mall_panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="10800" data-file-height="2468" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Northrop_Mall_panorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mall panorama, from left: Ford Hall, Coffman Memorial Union, Kolthoff Hall, Smith Hall (in center of image), Walter Library, Johnston Hall, Northrop, and Morrill Hall</div></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AerialUMN-MPLS012506.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/AerialUMN-MPLS012506.jpg/220px-AerialUMN-MPLS012506.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/AerialUMN-MPLS012506.jpg/330px-AerialUMN-MPLS012506.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/AerialUMN-MPLS012506.jpg/440px-AerialUMN-MPLS012506.jpg 2x" data-file-width="910" data-file-height="580" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AerialUMN-MPLS012506.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial photo of the Minneapolis campus, facing east</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UMN-NorthrupMall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/UMN-NorthrupMall.jpg/220px-UMN-NorthrupMall.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/UMN-NorthrupMall.jpg/330px-UMN-NorthrupMall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/UMN-NorthrupMall.jpg/440px-UMN-NorthrupMall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UMN-NorthrupMall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>East Bank</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walter_Library-20060904.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Walter_Library-20060904.jpg/220px-Walter_Library-20060904.jpg" width="220" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Walter_Library-20060904.jpg/330px-Walter_Library-20060904.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Walter_Library-20060904.jpg/440px-Walter_Library-20060904.jpg 2x" data-file-width="535" data-file-height="458" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walter_Library-20060904.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Walter_Library" title="Walter Library">Walter Library</a>, Northrop Mall</div></div></div>
<p>To help ease navigation of the large campus, the university has divided the <b>East Bank</b> into several areas: <b>the Knoll area</b>, <b>the Mall area</b>, <b>the Health area</b>, <b>the Athletic area</b>, and <b>the Gateway area</b>.
</p><p><b>The Knoll area</b>, the oldest part of the university's current location, is in the northwestern part of the campus.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Most <a href="/wiki/Discipline" title="Discipline">disciplines</a> in this area relate to the <a href="/wiki/Humanities" title="Humanities">humanities</a>. Burton Hall is home to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_College_of_Education_and_Human_Development" title="University of Minnesota College of Education and Human Development">College of Education and Human Development</a>. Many buildings in this area are well over 100 years old; a 13-building group comprises the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_Old_Campus_Historic_District" title="University of Minnesota Old Campus Historic District">Old Campus Historic District</a> on the U.S. <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> A residence hall, Sanford Hall, and a student-apartment complex, Roy Wilkins Hall, are in this area. The Institute for Advanced Study<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> is in the Nolte Center. This area is just south of the Dinkytown neighborhood and business area.
</p><p><b>Northrop Mall</b>, or <b>the Mall area</b>, is arguably the center of the Minneapolis campus. It was based on a design by <a href="/wiki/Cass_Gilbert" title="Cass Gilbert">Cass Gilbert</a>, although his plans were too extravagant to be fully implemented.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Several of the campus's primary buildings surround the Mall area. The <a href="/wiki/Northrop_Auditorium" title="Northrop Auditorium">Cyrus Northrop Memorial Auditorium</a> provides a northern anchor, with <a href="/wiki/Coffman_Memorial_Union" title="Coffman Memorial Union">Coffman Memorial Union</a> (CMU) to the south. Four of the larger buildings to the sides of it are the primary <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physics</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">chemistry</a> buildings, (Vincent Hall, Tate Laboratory and Smith Hall, respectively) and <a href="/wiki/Walter_Library" title="Walter Library">Walter Library</a>. The Mall area is home to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_College_of_Liberal_Arts" title="University of Minnesota College of Liberal Arts">College of Liberal Arts</a>, which is Minnesota's largest public or private college, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_Institute_of_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Minnesota Institute of Technology">College of Science and Engineering</a>. Behind CMU is another residence hall, Comstock Hall, and another student-apartment complex, Yudof Hall.
</p><p><b>The Health area</b> is to the southeast of the Mall area and focuses on undergraduate buildings for <a href="/wiki/Biological_science" class="mw-redirect" title="Biological science">biological-science</a> students, as well as homes to the College of <a href="/wiki/Pharmacy" title="Pharmacy">Pharmacy</a>, the School of <a href="/wiki/Nursing" title="Nursing">Nursing</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_School_of_Dentistry" title="University of Minnesota School of Dentistry">School of Dentistry</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_Medical_School" title="University of Minnesota Medical School">Medical School</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_School_of_Public_Health" title="University of Minnesota School of Public Health">School of Public Health</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fairview_Health_Services" title="Fairview Health Services">Fairview Hospitals and Clinics</a>. This complex of buildings forms what is known as the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_Medical_Center" title="University of Minnesota Medical Center">University of Minnesota Medical Center</a>. Part of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_College_of_Biological_Sciences" title="University of Minnesota College of Biological Sciences">College of Biological Sciences</a> is housed in this area.
</p><p><span id="Superblock"></span>Across the street from Fairview Hospital is an area known as the "Superblock", a four-city-block space comprising four residence halls (Pioneer, Frontier, Centennial and Territorial Halls). The Superblock is one of the most popular locations for on-campus housing because it has the largest concentration of students living on campus and has a multitude of social activities between the residence halls.
</p><p><b>The Athletic area</b> is directly north of the Superblock and includes four recreation/athletic facilities: the University Recreation Center, Cooke Hall, the University Fieldhouse, and the <a href="/wiki/Memorial_Stadium_(University_of_Minnesota)#University_Aquatic_center" title="Memorial Stadium (University of Minnesota)">University Aquatic Center</a>. These facilities are all connected by tunnels and skyways allowing students to use one locker-room facility. North of this complex is the <a href="/wiki/TCF_Bank_Stadium" title="TCF Bank Stadium">TCF Bank Stadium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Williams_Arena" title="Williams Arena">Williams Arena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mariucci_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Mariucci Arena">Mariucci Arena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ridder_Arena" title="Ridder Arena">Ridder Arena</a>, and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Baseline_Tennis_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Baseline Tennis Center (page does not exist)">Baseline Tennis Center</a>.
</p><p><b>The Gateway area</b>, an easternmost section, is primarily office buildings instead of classrooms and lecture halls. The most prominent building is <a href="/wiki/McNamara_Alumni_Center" title="McNamara Alumni Center">McNamara Alumni Center</a>. The university is also heavily invested in a <a href="/wiki/Biomedical" class="mw-redirect" title="Biomedical">biomedical-research</a> <a href="/wiki/Initiative_(enterprise)" title="Initiative (enterprise)">initiative</a> and has built five biomedical-research buildings that form a biomedical complex directly north of TCF Bank Stadium.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_architecture">Notable architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Notable architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pillsbury_Hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Pillsbury_Hall.jpg/220px-Pillsbury_Hall.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Pillsbury_Hall.jpg/330px-Pillsbury_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Pillsbury_Hall.jpg/440px-Pillsbury_Hall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pillsbury_Hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_Old_Campus_Historic_District#Pillsbury_Hall,_1889" title="University of Minnesota Old Campus Historic District">Pillsbury Hall</a>, one of the oldest buildings on campus (1889)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Weisman_Art_Museum.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Weisman_Art_Museum.jpg/220px-Weisman_Art_Museum.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Weisman_Art_Museum.jpg/330px-Weisman_Art_Museum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Weisman_Art_Museum.jpg/440px-Weisman_Art_Museum.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Weisman_Art_Museum.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Weisman_Art_Museum" title="Weisman Art Museum">Frederick R. Weisman Art Museum</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_Armory" title="University of Minnesota Armory">Armory</a>, northeast of the Northrop Mall, is built like a <a href="/wiki/Norman_architecture" title="Norman architecture">Norman</a> <a href="/wiki/Castle" title="Castle">castle</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/Sally_port" title="Sally port">sally-port</a> entrance facing Church Street, and a tower originally intended to be the Professor of <a href="/wiki/Military_Science" class="mw-redirect" title="Military Science">Military Science</a>'s residence, until it was found to be too cold. It originally held the athletics department as well as the military-science classes it now holds.
</p><p>One of the oldest buildings on campus is <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_Old_Campus_Historic_District#Pillsbury_Hall,_1889" title="University of Minnesota Old Campus Historic District">Pillsbury Hall</a>, designed in the <a href="/wiki/Richardsonian_Romanesque" title="Richardsonian Romanesque">Richardsonian Romanesque</a> style and built using varieties of sandstone available in Minnesota. It has a unique color that is hard to capture in a photograph. Many of the buildings on the East Bank campus were designed by the prolific Minnesota architect <a href="/wiki/Clarence_H._Johnston,_Sr." class="mw-redirect" title="Clarence H. Johnston, Sr.">Clarence Johnston</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Jacobean_architecture" title="Jacobean architecture">Jacobean</a> Folwell Hall and the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Renaissance" title="Roman Renaissance">Roman Renaissance</a> <a href="/wiki/Walter_Library" title="Walter Library">Walter Library</a>, which he considered the heart of the university.
</p><p>In more recent times, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Gehry" title="Frank Gehry">Frank Gehry</a> designed the <a href="/wiki/Weisman_Art_Museum" title="Weisman Art Museum">Frederick R. Weisman Art Museum</a>. It is a typical example of his work with curving metallic structures.
</p><p>Another new building is the addition to the Architecture building designed by <a href="/wiki/Steven_Holl" title="Steven Holl">Steven Holl</a> and completed in 2002. It won an <a href="/wiki/American_Institute_of_Architects" title="American Institute of Architects">American Institute of Architects</a> award for its innovative design. The Architecture building was then renamed Rapson Hall after the local <a href="/wiki/Modernist_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Modernist architecture">modernist</a> architect and School of Architecture Dean <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Rapson" title="Ralph Rapson">Ralph Rapson</a>.
</p><p>The university also has historic <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities">fraternities and sororities</a> buildings (a "Greek row") north of Northrop Mall on University Avenue SE. 
</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Fraternities_and_Sororities_at_the_University_of_Minnesota#Building_Fraternity_Row" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Fraternities and Sororities at the University of Minnesota">List of Fraternities and Sororities at the University of Minnesota §&#160;Building Fraternity Row</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="West_Bank">West Bank</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: West Bank">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rarig_Center-20071213.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Rarig_Center-20071213.jpg/220px-Rarig_Center-20071213.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Rarig_Center-20071213.jpg/330px-Rarig_Center-20071213.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Rarig_Center-20071213.jpg/440px-Rarig_Center-20071213.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rarig_Center-20071213.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Department of Theatre Arts &amp; Dance, Rarig Center</div></div></div>
<p>The <b>West Bank</b> covers 53 acres (21&#160;ha). The West Bank Arts Quarter includes:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Rarig_Center" title="Rarig Center">Rarig Center</a> (Theatre Arts &amp; Dance)</li>
<li>The Barbara Barker Center for Dance</li>
<li>Ferguson Hall (School of Music)</li>
<li>Ted Mann Concert Hall</li>
<li>Regis Center for Art</li></ul>
<p>The Quarter is home to several annual interdisciplinary arts festivals.
</p><p>The Social Sciences are also on the West Bank and include the <a href="/wiki/Carlson_School_of_Management" title="Carlson School of Management">Carlson School of Management</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_Law_School" title="University of Minnesota Law School">Law School</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Hubert_H._Humphrey_School_of_Public_Affairs" class="mw-redirect" title="Hubert H. Humphrey School of Public Affairs">Hubert H. Humphrey School of Public Affairs</a>.
</p><p>Wilson Library, the largest library in the university system, is also on the West Bank as is Middlebrook Hall, the largest residence hall on campus. Approximately 900 students reside in the building named in honor of William T. Middlebrook.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Getting_around">Getting around</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Getting around">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Washington_Avenue_Bridge_Minneapolis.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Washington_Avenue_Bridge_Minneapolis.jpg/220px-Washington_Avenue_Bridge_Minneapolis.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Washington_Avenue_Bridge_Minneapolis.jpg/330px-Washington_Avenue_Bridge_Minneapolis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Washington_Avenue_Bridge_Minneapolis.jpg/440px-Washington_Avenue_Bridge_Minneapolis.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="524" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Washington_Avenue_Bridge_Minneapolis.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Washington_Avenue_Bridge_(Minneapolis)" title="Washington Avenue Bridge (Minneapolis)">Washington Avenue Bridge</a> connects the East Bank and West Bank portions of the <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis" title="Minneapolis">Minneapolis</a> campus.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Green_Line,_Coffman_Union,_and_bus_stop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Green_Line%2C_Coffman_Union%2C_and_bus_stop.jpg/220px-Green_Line%2C_Coffman_Union%2C_and_bus_stop.jpg" width="220" height="90" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Green_Line%2C_Coffman_Union%2C_and_bus_stop.jpg/330px-Green_Line%2C_Coffman_Union%2C_and_bus_stop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Green_Line%2C_Coffman_Union%2C_and_bus_stop.jpg/440px-Green_Line%2C_Coffman_Union%2C_and_bus_stop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4335" data-file-height="1782" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Green_Line,_Coffman_Union,_and_bus_stop.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Green_Line_(Minnesota)" class="mw-redirect" title="Green Line (Minnesota)">Green Line</a> train after leaving the <a href="/wiki/East_Bank_(Metro_Transit_station)" class="mw-redirect" title="East Bank (Metro Transit station)">East Bank Station</a>, heading towards <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Minneapolis" class="mw-redirect" title="Downtown Minneapolis">Downtown Minneapolis</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Washington_Avenue_Bridge_(Minneapolis)" title="Washington Avenue Bridge (Minneapolis)">Washington Avenue Bridge</a> crossing the Mississippi River provides access between the East and West Banks, on foot, designated bike lanes, or via free shuttle service. The bridge has two separate <a href="/wiki/Deck_(bridge)" title="Deck (bridge)">decks</a>: the lower deck for vehicles and the newly constructed light rail, and the upper deck for pedestrian and bicycle traffic. An unheated enclosed walkway runs the length of the bridge and shelters students from the weather. Walking and riding bicycles are the most common modes of transportation among students. University Police occasionally cite individuals for <a href="/wiki/Jaywalking" title="Jaywalking">jaywalking</a> as well as riding bicycles on restricted sidewalk areas in areas surrounding the university resulting in fines as high as $250. This is often done at the beginning of a school year or after pedestrians interfere with traffic.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are some pedestrian tunnels to get from building to building during harsh weather; they are marked with signs reading "<a href="/wiki/The_Gopher_Way" title="The Gopher Way">The Gopher Way</a>".
</p><p>The Minneapolis campus is near <a href="/wiki/Interstate_Highway_System" title="Interstate Highway System">Interstates</a> <a href="/wiki/Interstate_94" title="Interstate 94">94</a> and <a href="/wiki/Interstate_35" title="Interstate 35">35W</a> and is bordered by the Minneapolis neighborhoods of <a href="/wiki/Dinkytown" title="Dinkytown">Dinkytown</a> (on the north), <a href="/wiki/Cedar-Riverside,_Minneapolis" title="Cedar-Riverside, Minneapolis">Cedar-Riverside</a> (on the west), <a href="/wiki/Stadium_Village" class="mw-redirect" title="Stadium Village">Stadium Village</a> (on the southeast), and <a href="/wiki/Prospect_Park,_Minneapolis" title="Prospect Park, Minneapolis">Prospect Park</a> (on the east).
</p><p>Three <a href="/wiki/Light_rail_in_Minnesota" class="mw-redirect" title="Light rail in Minnesota">light-rail stations</a> serve the university along the <a href="/wiki/Green_Line_(Minnesota)" class="mw-redirect" title="Green Line (Minnesota)">Green Line</a>. The stations include <a href="/wiki/Stadium_Village_(Metro_Transit_station)" class="mw-redirect" title="Stadium Village (Metro Transit station)">Stadium Village</a>, the <a href="/wiki/East_Bank_(Metro_Transit_station)" class="mw-redirect" title="East Bank (Metro Transit station)">East Bank</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/West_Bank_(Metro_Transit_station)" class="mw-redirect" title="West Bank (Metro Transit station)">West Bank</a>. The university partnered with <a href="/wiki/Metro_(Minnesota)" title="Metro (Minnesota)">Metro</a> to offer students, staff, and faculty members a <a href="/wiki/Go-To_card#Campus_Zone_Pass" title="Go-To card">Campus Zone Pass</a> that enables free travel on the three stations that pass through campus,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> as well as a discounted unlimited pass for students.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="St._Paul_campus">St. Paul campus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: St. Paul campus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AerialUMN-SP012506.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/AerialUMN-SP012506.jpg/220px-AerialUMN-SP012506.jpg" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/AerialUMN-SP012506.jpg/330px-AerialUMN-SP012506.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/AerialUMN-SP012506.jpg/440px-AerialUMN-SP012506.jpg 2x" data-file-width="780" data-file-height="463" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AerialUMN-SP012506.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial photo of St. Paul campus, facing south</div></div></div>
<p>The St. Paul campus is in the city of <a href="/wiki/Falcon_Heights,_Minnesota" title="Falcon Heights, Minnesota">Falcon Heights</a>, about 3 miles (4.8&#160;km) away from the Minneapolis campus. The default place name for the ZIP code serving the campus is "St. Paul", but "Falcon Heights" is also recognized for use in the street addresses of all campus buildings. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_College_of_Food,_Agricultural_and_Natural_Resource_Sciences" title="University of Minnesota College of Food, Agricultural and Natural Resource Sciences">College of Food, Agricultural and Natural Resource Sciences</a>, including the University of Minnesota Food Industry Center and many other disciplines from social sciences to <a href="/wiki/Vocational_education" title="Vocational education">vocational education</a> are on this campus. This also includes the College of Continuing and Professional Studies,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> College of Veterinary Medicine,<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> and the College of Biological Sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The extensive lawns, flowers, trees, woods, and the surrounding University research farm plots creates a greener and quieter campus. It has a grassy mall of its own and can be a bit of a retreat from the more-urban Minneapolis campus. Prominent on this campus is Bailey Hall, the St. Paul campus' only residence hall. There are campus connectors running every 5 minutes on the weekdays when school is in session, and every 20 minutes on weekends, allowing students easy access to both campuses.
</p><p>The Continuing Education and Conference Center,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> which serves over 20,000 conference attendees per year, is also on the St. Paul campus.
</p><p>The St. Paul campus is home to the College of Design's department of Design, Housing, and Apparel (DHA). Located in McNeal Hall, DHA includes the departmental disciplines of Apparel Design, Graphic Design, Housing Studies, Interior Design, and Retail Merchandising.
</p><p>The St. Paul campus is known to University students and staff for the Dairy Salesroom,<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> which sells food (including ice cream) produced in the university's state-certified dairy plant by students, faculty and staff, and the similar Meat Sales Room.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The St. Paul campus borders the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_State_Fair" title="Minnesota State Fair">Minnesota State Fairgrounds</a>, which hosts the largest <a href="/wiki/State_fair" title="State fair">state fair</a> in the United States by daily attendance.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The fair lasts twelve days, from late August through Labor Day in early September. The grounds also serve a variety of functions during the rest of the year.
</p><p>Although the Falcon Heights <a href="/wiki/North_American_Numbering_Plan" title="North American Numbering Plan">area code</a> is 651, the university telephone system trunk lines use Minneapolis <a href="/wiki/Telephone_exchange" title="Telephone exchange">exchanges</a> and its 612 area code.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Commuting_between_Minneapolis_and_St._Paul_campuses">Commuting between Minneapolis and St. Paul campuses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Commuting between Minneapolis and St. Paul campuses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the school year on regular weekdays, the Campus Connectors operate with schedule-less service as often as every five minutes during the busiest parts of the school day between 7:00am and 5:30pm, slowing to once every 15 or 20 minutes during earlier or later hours.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The estimated time to commute from St. Paul to East Bank is 15 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, the system carried 3.55 million riders. Despite the fact the shuttle service is free, it is comparatively inexpensive to operate: with an operating cost of $4.55 million in 2008, the operating subsidy was only $1.28 per passenger. Even <a href="/wiki/Metro_Transit_(Minnesota)" title="Metro Transit (Minnesota)">Metro Transit</a>'s busy <a href="/wiki/METRO_(Minnesota)" class="mw-redirect" title="METRO (Minnesota)">METRO</a> <a href="/wiki/Blue_Line_(Minnesota)" class="mw-redirect" title="Blue Line (Minnesota)">Blue Line</a> light rail required a subsidy of $1.44 that year, and that was with many riders paying $1.75 or more for a ride.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus_safety">Campus safety</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Campus safety">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Step Up campaign is a program that helps students prevent crimes, sexual assault, and excessive drinking by teaching students how to intervene and prevent in a positive way.<sup id="cite_ref-Step_Up_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Step_Up-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> They do this by explaining the <a href="/wiki/Bystander_effect" title="Bystander effect">Bystander effect</a>. The U of M also has a TXT-U emergency notification text messaging system that sends out a notification to all faculty, staff, and students in case of emergency.<sup id="cite_ref-TXT_-_U_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TXT_-_U-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Similarly, there are different resources which students are able to get help while getting home. 624-WALK, an escort to walk to adjacent campuses and neighborhoods, and Gopher Chauffeur, a van service that offers rides near and on campus. Both of these are free and open to all students, staff, and faculty.<sup id="cite_ref-Creating_a_safe_U_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Creating_a_safe_U-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In addition, there are almost 200 AED's on campus and 200 yellow phones for emergency only calls. The University Police Station has 20 Code Blue Phones around campus that immediately connect people to their office. There are also over 2,000 security cameras being monitored 24 hours a day.<sup id="cite_ref-Creating_a_safe_U_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Creating_a_safe_U-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sexual_assaults">Sexual assaults</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Sexual assaults">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>More than 1,000 sexual assaults on campus were reported between the years 2010 and 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-Tribune_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tribune-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>  The total number of prosecutions for rape was zero according to Katie Eichele of the Aurora Center,<sup id="cite_ref-Tribune_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tribune-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> until the conviction of <a href="/wiki/2014_University_of_Minnesota_rape_case" title="2014 University of Minnesota rape case">Daniel Drill-Mellum</a> in 2016, for the rapes of two fellow students.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>  Of the sexual assaults on campus, few are reported to university police.<sup id="cite_ref-Fox9_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fox9-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>  Six resulted in arrest from 2010 to 2015; one was determined to be unfounded.<sup id="cite_ref-Fox9_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fox9-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> In a study by campus police, in the years between 2005 and 2015, sexual assaults at the university remained the same or increased<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> despite six sexual assault resources and many anti-crime programs on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_record">Environmental record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Environmental record">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small><i>(May 2018)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Another building that has won an award is Robert H. Bruininks Hall, originally named Science Teaching and Student Services (STSS) at its opening in August 2010. This building has been awarded the prestigious LEED Gold certification. LEED, or <a href="/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design" title="Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design">Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design</a>, is an internationally recognized <a href="/wiki/Green_building" title="Green building">green building</a> certification system administered by the U.S. Green Building Council. LEED measures multiple dimensions of a building's design and construction including <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_sites" class="mw-redirect" title="Sustainable sites">sustainable sites</a>, energy and atmosphere, materials and resources, <a href="/wiki/Water_efficiency" title="Water efficiency">water efficiency</a>, and indoor environmental quality.
</p><p>"It's appropriate that a building that supports science education and overlooks a great river would be built with principles of sustainability at the forefront," said, U of M President Robert Bruininks at the opening of the building in August 2010.
</p><p>Highlights of sustainability in Bruininks Hall include:
</p>
<ul><li>Conserving water— Installation of low-flow sinks and bathroom fixtures that use 50 percent less water than a typical building of its size. Outdoor irrigation systems use a monitoring system that measures ground saturation and local weather patterns, so irrigation only takes place when needed.  Native, drought tolerant plants reduce runoff to the river and minimize irrigation needs.</li>
<li>Recycling and reuse— Builders reused sections of the foundation from the Science Classroom Building that occupied the site to construct Bruininks Hall. This saved time and money and reduced the amount of new materials used to build it. Recycled materials were incorporated into the carpet, tables, chairs and structural steel. In addition, 94 percent of the construction debris from the site was diverted from the landfill for reuse or recycling.</li>
<li>Air quality and air flow— An innovative underfloor air distribution system allows fresh air to move into the building while pushing stale air to the ceiling. This air is then collected in air ducts and circulated outside, providing healthy and comfortable air for occupants.</li>
<li>Exterior glass— The exterior glass on the west and south sides of the building provides an aesthetically pleasing view of the river and downtown and also provides natural lighting. This feature proved challenging for those designing an energy efficient structure. They found a solution with a custom-designed white dot pattern on the glass and strategically placed columns to maximize views, minimize glare and reduce solar heat gain by 50 percent.</li>
<li>Building materials— When possible, builders used construction materials manufactured within a 500-mile radius of Minneapolis to reduce transportation emissions and to support the regional economy.</li>
<li>Connections— Bruininks Hall further facilitates connections to alternative transportation and the Mississippi River through its design and structure. Bike racks around the building provide adequate parking. Bus stops are conveniently near the building.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Big_Ten_Academic_Alliance">Big Ten Academic Alliance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Big Ten Academic Alliance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The University of Minnesota is a participant in the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Academic_Alliance" title="Big Ten Academic Alliance">Big Ten Academic Alliance</a>. The Big Ten Academic Alliance (BTAA) is the academic consortium of the universities in the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a>. Engaging in $10 billion in research in 2014-2015, BTAA universities provide powerful insight into important issues in medicine, technology, agriculture, and communities. Students at participating schools are also allowed "in-house" borrowing privileges at other schools' libraries.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The BTAA uses collective purchasing and licensing, and has saved member institutions $19 million to date.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Course sharing,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Professional_development" title="Professional development">professional development</a> programs,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Study_abroad" class="mw-redirect" title="Study abroad">study abroad</a> and international collaborations,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> and other initiatives are also part of the BTAA.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life_and_traditions">Student life and traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Student life and traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="Greek_life.2C_professional_and_honor_societies"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Greek_life,_professional_and_honor_societies">Greek life, professional and honor societies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Greek life, professional and honor societies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_fraternities_and_sororities_at_the_University_of_Minnesota" title="List of fraternities and sororities at the University of Minnesota">List of fraternities and sororities at the University of Minnesota</a></div>
<p>The number of fraternities and sororities at the University of Minnesota is extensive. Including defunct branches, the Greek System numbers more than 200 organizations. More than half of these remain active today, whose pioneers have had a presence on the Twin Cities campus for over 145 years.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The university's Greek societies include the highly visible residential <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities_in_North_America" class="mw-redirect" title="Fraternities and sororities in North America">Academic and Social</a> chapters whose numbers include non-residential multicultural groups. The Greek System extends to include <a href="/wiki/Professional_fraternities_and_sororities" title="Professional fraternities and sororities">Professional Fraternities</a>, <a href="/wiki/Honor_society" title="Honor society">Honor Societies</a>, Religious and <a href="/wiki/Service_fraternities_and_sororities" title="Service fraternities and sororities">Service Fraternities</a>. Many have built and occupy historically significant "Fraternity Row" homes along University Ave. SE, 10th Ave. SE, 4th Street SE, and 5th Street SE, all in Minneapolis, or along Cleveland Ave. near the St. Paul campus.<sup id="cite_ref-HistoricalStudy2003_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistoricalStudy2003-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Greek System participants are more likely to graduate than the average undergraduate student, are more likely to graduate with a higher GPA, and Greek alumni consistently contribute more financial support to the University than other alumni sectors.<sup id="cite_ref-GCSTF12_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GCSTF12-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SODC1987_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SODC1987-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GVPresentation_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GVPresentation-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OFSL2017_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OFSL2017-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> As of June 2018, approximately 3,900 system members made up about 11% of the campus population. Minnesota hosts 38 academic fraternities, 20 academic sororities, 56 honors societies, 31 professional societies, and two service-focused chapters.<sup id="cite_ref-OFSL2017_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OFSL2017-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Northrupmall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Northrupmall.jpg/170px-Northrupmall.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Northrupmall.jpg/255px-Northrupmall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Northrupmall.jpg/340px-Northrupmall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2472" data-file-height="3296" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Northrupmall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The eastern edge of the Northrop Mall, Spring 2008</div></div></div>
