<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Print">Print</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Print">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Daily" title="Minnesota Daily">The Minnesota Daily</a></i> is published only twice a week during the normal school season as of the Fall 2016 semester.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> It is printed once each week during the summer. The <i>Daily</i> is operated by an autonomous organization run entirely by students. It was first published on May 1, 1900. Outside of every day news coverage the paper has also published special issues such as the Grapevine Awards, Ski-U-Mah, the Bar &amp; Beer Guide, Sex-U-Mah, and others.
</p><p>A long-defunct but fondly remembered humor magazine, <i><a href="/wiki/Ski-U-Mah_(magazine)" title="Ski-U-Mah (magazine)">Ski-U-Mah</a></i>, was published from about 1930 to 1950. It launched the career of novelist and scriptwriter <a href="/wiki/Max_Shulman" title="Max Shulman">Max Shulman</a>.
</p><p>A relative newcomer to the university's print-media community is <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wake_Student_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="The Wake Student Magazine">The Wake Student Magazine</a></i>, a weekly magazine that covers University-related stories and provides a forum for student expression. It was founded in November 2001 in an effort to diversify campus media and achieved student group status in February 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-fund_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fund-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Students from many disciplines do all of the reporting, writing, editing, illustration, photography, layout and business management for the publication. The magazine was founded by James DeLong and Chris Ruen.<sup id="cite_ref-dead_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dead-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Wake</i> was named the nation's best campus publication (2006) by the Independent Press Association.<sup id="cite_ref-fund_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fund-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Additionally, the <i>Wake</i> publishes <i>Liminal</i>, a literary journal that began in 2005. <i>Liminal</i> was created in the absence of an undergraduate literary journal and continues to bring poetry and prose to the university community.
</p><p><i>The Wake</i> has faced a number of challenges during its existence, due in part to the reliance on student fees funding. In April 2004, the needed $60,000 in funding was restored, which allowed for the magazine's continued existence after the Student Services Fees Committee had initially declined to fund it.<sup id="cite_ref-dead_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dead-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> They faced further challenges in 2005 when their request for additional funding to publish weekly was denied<sup id="cite_ref-dead2_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dead2-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> and then partially restored.<sup id="cite_ref-dead4_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dead4-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2005 conservatives on campus began formulating a new monthly magazine named <i>The</i> <i>Minnesota Republic</i>. The first issue was released in February 2006, and funding by student service fees started in September 2006.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">Radio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Radio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The campus radio station, <a href="/wiki/KUOM" title="KUOM">KUOM</a> "Radio K", broadcasts an eclectic variety of <a href="/wiki/Independent_music" title="Independent music">independent music</a> during the day on 770 <a href="/wiki/KHz" class="mw-redirect" title="KHz">kHz</a> <a href="/wiki/AM_radio" class="mw-redirect" title="AM radio">AM</a>. Its 5,000-watt signal has a range of 80 miles (130&#160;km), but shuts down at dusk because of <a href="/wiki/Federal_Communications_Commission" title="Federal Communications Commission">Federal Communications Commission</a> regulations. In 2003, the station added a low-power (8-watt) signal on 106.5&#160;MHz <a href="/wiki/FM_radio" class="mw-redirect" title="FM radio">FM</a> overnight and on weekends. In 2005, a 10-watt translator began broadcasting from Falcon Heights on 100.7 FM at all times. Radio K also <a href="/wiki/Internet_radio" title="Internet radio">streams</a> its content at www.radiok.org. With roots in experimental transmissions that began before World War I, the station received the first AM broadcast license in the state on January 13, 1922, and began broadcasting as <a href="/wiki/Radio_K" class="mw-redirect" title="Radio K">WLB</a>, changing to the KUOM <a href="/wiki/Radio_call_sign" class="mw-redirect" title="Radio call sign">call sign</a> about two decades later. The station had an educational format until 1993 when it merged with a smaller campus-only music station to become what is now known as Radio K. A small group of full-time employees are joined by over 20 part-time student employees who oversee the station. Most of the on-air talent consists of student volunteers.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Some television programs made on campus have been broadcast on local <a href="/wiki/Public_Broadcasting_Service" class="mw-redirect" title="Public Broadcasting Service">PBS</a> station <a href="/wiki/KTCI" class="mw-redirect" title="KTCI">KTCI</a> channel 17. Several episodes of <i>Great Conversations</i> have been made since 2002, featuring one-on-one discussions between University faculty and experts brought in from around the world. <i>Tech Talk</i> is a show meant to help people who feel intimidated by modern technology, including cellular phones and computers.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Minnesota_Student_Association">Minnesota Student Association</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Minnesota Student Association">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Minnesota Student Association (MSA) is the undergraduate student government at the University of Minnesota. It advocates for student interests on local, state, and federal levels, and focuses on efforts that directly benefit student population.
</p><p>"Gopher Chauffeur," originally titled the MSA Express, is a student-operated late-night ride service.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Piloted by MSA, the 2007–2008 administration of Emma Olson and Ross Skattum began the process of transitioning the service to the university's Boynton Health Services.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> This was done to ensure its longevity. Student response was overwhelmingly positive,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> and the program was expanded in recent years due to campus safety concerns.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>MSA was instrumental in passing legislation in the 2013 Minnesota legislature for medical amnesty, and has focused more heavily on legislative advocacy in recent years.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Graduate_and_Professional_Student_Assembly">Graduate and Professional Student Assembly</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Graduate and Professional Student Assembly">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Graduate and Professional Student Assembly (GAPSA) is responsible for graduate and professional student governance at the University of Minnesota. It is the largest and most comprehensive graduate/professional student governance organization in the United States. GAPSA serves students in the <a href="/wiki/Carlson_School_of_Management" title="Carlson School of Management">Carlson School of Management</a>, the Dental School, the Graduate School, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_Law_School" title="University of Minnesota Law School">Law School</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_Medical_School" title="University of Minnesota Medical School">Medical School</a>, the School of Nursing, the College of Pharmacy, the School of Public Health, the College of Veterinary Medicine, and the <a href="/wiki/College_of_Education_and_Human_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="College of Education and Human Development">College of Education and Human Development</a>. GAPSA is also a member of the National Association of Graduate-Professional Students.
</p><p>The University of Minnesota has the second largest number of graduate and professional students in the United States at over 16,000. All registered <a href="/wiki/Graduate_student" class="mw-redirect" title="Graduate student">graduate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Professional_students" class="mw-redirect" title="Professional students">professional students</a> at the University of Minnesota are members of GAPSA. It was established in 1990 as a non-profit (IRS 501 (c)(3)) confederation of independent college councils representing all graduate and professional students at the University of Minnesota to the Board of Regents, the President of the University, the University Senate, the university at large and wider community. GAPSA serves as a resource for member councils, as the primary contact point for administrative units, as a graduate and professional student policy-making and policy-influencing body, and as a center of intercollegiate and intra-collegiate interaction among students.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Minnesota's athletic teams at the Twin Cities campus are known as the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Golden_Gophers" title="Minnesota Golden Gophers">Minnesota Golden Gophers</a> and compete in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">Division I</a> as members of the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a>. They have won 20 national championships as of 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Golden_Gophers" title="Minnesota Golden Gophers">Minnesota Golden Gophers</a></div>
<p>The university's intercollegiate sports teams are called the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Golden_Gophers" title="Minnesota Golden Gophers">Golden Gophers</a> and are members of the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Western_Collegiate_Hockey_Association" title="Western Collegiate Hockey Association">Western Collegiate Hockey Association</a> (WCHA) in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">National Collegiate Athletic Association</a> (NCAA). Since the 2013–14 school year, the only Minnesota team that does not compete in the Big Ten is the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Golden_Gophers_women%27s_ice_hockey" title="Minnesota Golden Gophers women&#39;s ice hockey">women's ice hockey team</a>, which competes in the WCHA. The Gophers <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Golden_Gophers_men%27s_ice_hockey" title="Minnesota Golden Gophers men&#39;s ice hockey">men's ice hockey team</a> was a longtime WCHA member, but left when the Big Ten began operating a <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference#Men&#39;s_ice_hockey" title="Big Ten Conference">men's ice hockey league</a> with six inaugural members. The current athletic director is Mark Coyle, who took the position from interim athletic director <a href="/wiki/Beth_Goetz" title="Beth Goetz">Beth Goetz</a>, after <a href="/wiki/Norwood_Teague" title="Norwood Teague">Norwood Teague</a> resigned in August 2015 amid sexual assault allegations. Teague replaced <a href="/wiki/Joel_Maturi" title="Joel Maturi">Joel Maturi</a>.
</p><p>The Golden Gophers' most notable rivalry is the annual college football game against the <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_Badgers" title="Wisconsin Badgers">Wisconsin Badgers</a> (<a href="/wiki/University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison" title="University of Wisconsin–Madison">University of Wisconsin–Madison</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madison,_Wisconsin" title="Madison, Wisconsin">Madison</a>, Wisconsin) for <a href="/wiki/Paul_Bunyan%27s_Axe" class="mw-redirect" title="Paul Bunyan&#39;s Axe">Paul Bunyan's Axe</a>, the longest continuous rivalry in <a href="/wiki/NCAA" class="mw-redirect" title="NCAA">NCAA</a> Division I football. The two universities also compete in the Border Battle, a year-long athletic competition in which each sport season is worth 40 points divided by the number of times the teams play each other (i.e. football is worth 40 points because they play each other only once, while women's ice hockey is worth 10 points per game because they play four times a year). Conference and post-season <a href="/wiki/Playoffs" title="Playoffs">playoffs</a> do not count in the point standings.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Goldy_Gopher" title="Goldy Gopher">Goldy Gopher</a> is the mascot for the Twin Cities campus and the associated sports teams. The <a href="/wiki/Gopher_(animal)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gopher (animal)">gopher</a> mascot is a tradition as old as the state which was tabbed the "Gopher State" in 1857 after a political cartoon ridiculing the US$5-million railroad loan which helped open up the West. The cartoon portrayed shifty railroad barons as striped gophers pulling a railroad car carrying the Territorial Legislature. Later, the university picked up the nickname with the first university <a href="/wiki/Yearbook" title="Yearbook">yearbook</a> bearing the name "Gopher Annual" appearing in 1887.
</p><p>The "<a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Rouser" title="Minnesota Rouser">Minnesota Rouser</a>" is the University of Minnesota's <a href="/wiki/Fight_song" title="Fight song">fight song</a>. It is commonly played and sung by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_Marching_Band" title="University of Minnesota Marching Band">Minnesota Marching Band</a>, the university's 320-member <a href="/wiki/Marching_band" title="Marching band">marching band</a>, at various events such as <a href="/wiki/Graduation" title="Graduation">commencement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Convocation" title="Convocation">convocation</a>, and athletic games. It is among a number of songs associated with the university, including the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_March" title="Minnesota March">Minnesota March</a>, which was composed for the university by <a href="/wiki/John_Philip_Sousa" title="John Philip Sousa">John Philip Sousa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hail!_Minnesota" title="Hail! Minnesota">Hail! Minnesota</a>, the university's <a href="/wiki/Alma_mater_(song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Alma mater (song)">alma mater</a> and <a href="/wiki/State_song" class="mw-redirect" title="State song">state song</a> of Minnesota.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Golden_Gophers_football" title="Minnesota Golden Gophers football">Minnesota Golden Gophers football</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TCF_Bank_Stadium_opener.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/TCF_Bank_Stadium_opener.jpg/220px-TCF_Bank_Stadium_opener.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/TCF_Bank_Stadium_opener.jpg/330px-TCF_Bank_Stadium_opener.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/TCF_Bank_Stadium_opener.jpg/440px-TCF_Bank_Stadium_opener.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TCF_Bank_Stadium_opener.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/TCF_Bank_Stadium" title="TCF Bank Stadium">TCF Bank Stadium</a> replaced the <a href="/wiki/Hubert_H._Humphrey_Metrodome" title="Hubert H. Humphrey Metrodome">Hubert H. Humphrey Metrodome</a> as the Gophers' home stadium in 2009.</div></div></div>
<p>The Minnesota Golden Gophers are one of the oldest programs in college-football history. They have won 7 <a href="/wiki/National_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="National Championship">National Championships</a> and 18 <a href="/wiki/List_of_Big_Ten_National_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Big Ten National Championships">Big Ten Conference Championships</a>. The Golden Gophers played their first game on September 29, 1882, a 4–0 victory over <a href="/wiki/Hamline_University" title="Hamline University">Hamline University</a>, St. Paul. In 1887, the Golden Gophers played host to the Wisconsin Badgers in a 63–0 victory. With the exception of 1906, the Golden Gophers and the Badgers have played each other every year since. The 124 games played against each other is the most-played rivalry in NCAA Division I FBS college football.
</p><p>In 1981, the Golden Gophers played their last game in <a href="/wiki/Memorial_Stadium_(University_of_Minnesota)" title="Memorial Stadium (University of Minnesota)">Memorial Stadium</a>. Between 1982 and 2008, the school hosted their home games in the <a href="/wiki/Hubert_H._Humphrey_Metrodome" title="Hubert H. Humphrey Metrodome">Hubert H. Humphrey Metrodome</a> in downtown Minneapolis until they moved back to campus on September 12, 2009, when their new home, <a href="/wiki/TCF_Bank_Stadium" title="TCF Bank Stadium">TCF Bank Stadium</a>, opened with a game against the <a href="/wiki/2009_Air_Force_Falcons_football_team" title="2009 Air Force Falcons football team">Air Force Falcons</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force_Academy" title="United States Air Force Academy">U.S. Air Force Academy</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Basketball">Basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Basketball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Golden_Gophers_men%27s_basketball" title="Minnesota Golden Gophers men&#39;s basketball">Minnesota Golden Gophers men's basketball</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Golden_Gophers_women%27s_basketball" title="Minnesota Golden Gophers women&#39;s basketball">Minnesota Golden Gophers women's basketball</a></div>
<p>The Golden Gophers men's basketball team has won two <a href="/wiki/Helms_Athletic_Foundation#NCAA_Basketball_National_Champions" title="Helms Athletic Foundation">National Championships</a>, two <a href="/wiki/National_Invitation_Tournament" title="National Invitation Tournament">National Invitation Tournament</a> (NIT) Championships and eight Big Ten Regular Season Championships. They also have six <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="NCAA Men&#39;s Division I Basketball Championship">NCAA Tournament</a>, including a <a href="/wiki/Final_Four" class="mw-redirect" title="Final Four">Final Four</a> appearance in 1997 and three <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="NCAA Men&#39;s Division I Basketball Championship">Sweet 16</a> appearances. However, because of <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_basketball_scandal" title="University of Minnesota basketball scandal">NCAA sanctions for academic fraud</a>, all postseason appearances from 1994 to 1998—in the NCAA Tournament in 1994, 1995, and 1997 and NIT in 1996 and 1998—were vacated. Most recently in April 2014, the Golden Gophers defeated SMU to win the NIT championship at Madison Square Garden in New York City.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Golden_Gophers" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Gophers">Golden Gophers</a> women's basketball team has enjoyed success in recent years under <a href="/wiki/Pam_Borton" title="Pam Borton">Pam Borton</a>, including a <a href="/wiki/Final_Four" class="mw-redirect" title="Final Four">Final Four</a> appearance in 2004. Overall, they have six <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Women%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="NCAA Women&#39;s Division I Basketball Championship">NCAA Tournament</a> appearances and three <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Women%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="NCAA Women&#39;s Division I Basketball Championship">Sweet 16</a> appearances.
</p>
<h4><span id="Men.27s_ice_hockey"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Men's_ice_hockey">Men's ice hockey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Men&#039;s ice hockey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Golden_Gophers_men%27s_ice_hockey" title="Minnesota Golden Gophers men&#39;s ice hockey">Minnesota Golden Gophers men's ice hockey</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mariucci_Arena.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Mariucci_Arena.jpg/220px-Mariucci_Arena.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Mariucci_Arena.jpg/330px-Mariucci_Arena.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Mariucci_Arena.jpg/440px-Mariucci_Arena.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="525" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mariucci_Arena.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mariucci_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Mariucci Arena">Mariucci Arena</a></div></div></div>
<p>Ice hockey is one of the most strongly supported athletic programs at the University of Minnesota, referred to by the university as "Minnesota's Pride on Ice."<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The high amount of support is due to the State of Minnesota's high affinity for the sport of ice hockey at all levels.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Golden Gophers men's ice-hockey program has won five <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Ice_Hockey_Championship#NCAA_Men&#39;s_Division_I_Ice_Hockey_Championship" title="NCAA Men&#39;s Ice Hockey Championship">Division I National Championships</a> and 13 <a href="/wiki/Western_Collegiate_Hockey_Association_men%27s_champions" title="Western Collegiate Hockey Association men&#39;s champions">Western Collegiate Hockey Association (WCHA) Regular Season Championships</a>, most recently in 2012. They have won 14 <a href="/wiki/Western_Collegiate_Hockey_Association_men%27s_champions" title="Western Collegiate Hockey Association men&#39;s champions">WCHA Tournament Championships</a> and have 20 NCAA <a href="/wiki/Frozen_Four" class="mw-redirect" title="Frozen Four">Frozen Four</a> appearances. A Golden Gophers hockey tradition is to stock the roster almost exclusively (sometimes completely) with Minnesota natives. Home games are played at Mariucci Arena. The Golden Gophers' big rivals are the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison" title="University of Wisconsin–Madison">University of Wisconsin–Madison</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Dakota" title="University of North Dakota">University of North Dakota</a>.
</p>
<h4><span id="Women.27s_hockey"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Women's_hockey">Women's hockey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Women&#039;s hockey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Golden_Gophers_women%27s_ice_hockey" title="Minnesota Golden Gophers women&#39;s ice hockey">Minnesota Golden Gophers women's ice hockey</a></div>
<p>The Golden Gophers women's hockey team has also won six National Championships, most recently in 2016, and six WCHA Regular Season Championships. They have also won four WCHA Tournament Championships and have eleven NCAA Frozen Four appearances. They play their home games in <a href="/wiki/Ridder_Arena" title="Ridder Arena">Ridder Arena</a>. They were the first collegiate women's hockey team to play in an arena dedicated solely to women's ice hockey. In the 2012–2013 season they finished undefeated at 41–0, and are the first and only NCAA Women's Hockey team to do so. After winning the NCAA tournament their winning streak stood at 49 games, dating back to February 17, 2012 when they lost to North Dakota.
</p>
<h4><span id="Women.27s_Rugby"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Women's_Rugby">Women's Rugby</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Minnesota&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Women&#039;s Rugby">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Golden Gophers Women's Rugby club team won the Midwest conference championships in 2015, 2016 and 2017.
</p>

<li id="cite_note-49"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-49">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Middlebrook served the University as Comptroller, VP of Business Administration, and was a longtime Secretary of the Board of Regents. He wrote a seminal text on estimating building needs for colleges and universities. Middlebrook graduated from <a href="/wiki/Dartmouth_College" title="Dartmouth College">Dartmouth College</a> in 1912, where he was a member of <a href="/wiki/Phi_Sigma_Kappa" title="Phi Sigma Kappa">Phi Sigma Kappa</a>.</span>
